  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b65f5668-ccb0-415e-9a20-f899b7e1975f'
      });
    }

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Its a really good series and I have a feeling the books might even be better than the show. There's a few different editions for it, so you can get a <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Its a really good series and I have a feeling the books might even be better than the show. There's a few different editions for it, so you can get a smaller one and try it out without having to buy omibus or anything. its also finished so no waiting around for a writer on the next one! art is great and its not over the top complicated, Id say its a great series for someone who is just starting with Graphic novels. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_691').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

  <span id="freeText6662608553522708639" style="display:none"><b>2020</b><br><br>I'm re-reading the books because we just watched the Netflix show and it made me think about how much I loved this story. This is <i>still</i> one of my all-time favorite graphic novels and if you haven't read it yet, I honestly can't recommend it enough.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581172651ra/28926353.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>2018</b><br>I was gifted the <i>beautiful</i> hardback set of these a while back and just finished re-reading the first book...again. Can't believe how much I'd forgotten! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515783803i/24870395.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The gist is that the violent murder of their father by two teens sends the three children and their mother to their dad's ancestral home. <br><b>Keyhouse.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515784228i/24870401._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Layer by layer the story of why their father was killed, what happened to them during the time the killers were in their house, and how the family is coping, starts coming together to paint a heart-wrenching tale. Then add a layer of mystery to the house itself, with its strange and magical <i>keys</i> that keep popping up, and you've got something amazing to read. <br>Because there's a secret history to everything their father had long ago forgotten about the house, and the youngest child, Bode, is starting to discover it all over again.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515784229i/24870402._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And fuck! It's creepy as hell!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431479337i/14840220._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Locke &amp; Key easily makes my Top 10 favorite graphic novel series. It's just one of the better-written stories, horror or otherwise, out there.<br><b>Highly recommended!</b><br><br>Older reviews - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <b>Re-read 2015</b><br>Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12058788-d-2" rel="nofollow noopener">Dᴀɴ 2.☢’s </a> for letting me read your copy of this one!<br><br>For some odd reason, I only gave this 4 stars the first time around. Not sure what I was thinking? This was fantastic! All 5 stars!<br>Have you read this series yet?<br>If not, DO IT!<br><br><b>Original review 2012</b><br>This is the first thing I've read by Joe Hill, and I have to say that I'm very impressed. The dialogue was amazing, and the characters felt quite real, especially for a graphic novel.<br>What seems to be a story about a family dealing with a terrible tragedy, slowly unfolds into something <i>more</i>. <br><i><b>Brrrrr</b></i>.<br>The artwork perfectly complements the creeptastic storyline in this. What else can I say? The entire thing was very well done, and I've heard from several sources that it only gets better from here on out. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_113594413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113594413" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113594413?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=weird-and-new-weird">weird-and-new-weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113594413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5032579015622518053">You can <b>color me SOLD</b> on this series.<br/><br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&current=LKCover-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695163.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Here's another intelligent, <b>strongly written</b> story with which to <b>pummel</b> the <b>perceptions</b> of the elitist <b>book snobbers</b>, who <b>sneer</b> and <b>snide</b> at the graphic novel medium. <br/><br/>To them, I <b>politely</b> say, "<b>BITE ME</b>"...because this is great stuff. <br/><br/>I was excited to read this because it was written by Joe Hill, the talented offspring of a certain literary <b>King</b> who shall remain <s>nameless</s> <b>Stephen</b>. While I thought Hill’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025.Heart_Shaped_Box' title='Heart-Shaped Box by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heart-Shaped Box</a> was a promising first work, I really f</span>
  <span id="freeText5032579015622518053" style="display:none">You can <b>color me SOLD</b> on this series.<br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=LKCover-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695163.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Here's another intelligent, <b>strongly written</b> story with which to <b>pummel</b> the <b>perceptions</b> of the elitist <b>book snobbers</b>, who <b>sneer</b> and <b>snide</b> at the graphic novel medium. <br><br>To them, I <b>politely</b> say, "<b>BITE ME</b>"...because this is great stuff. <br><br>I was excited to read this because it was written by Joe Hill, the talented offspring of a certain literary <b>King</b> who shall remain <s>nameless</s> <b>Stephen</b>. While I thought Hill’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025.Heart_Shaped_Box" title="Heart-Shaped Box by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart-Shaped Box</a> was a promising first work, I really fell enamored with him after reading his second, and much stronger, novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns" title="Horns by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Horns</a>. That effort definitively showed that Hill has story-telling chops, and I’ve been a Joe Hill enthusiast ever since. <br><br>So, I expected to enjoy this.<br><br>What I didn’t count on, was how wonderfully in step Gabriel Rodriquez’s art would be with Hill’s words, and how gracefully the two would play off each other, enhancing the already impressive quality of their individual efforts. This was dance. <br><br>Locke and Key is horror done by two artists who knew exactly what they wanted to accomplish...and did so. This is terror created through atmosphere, suspense and narrative, without simply resorting to the shock value of extreme, over-the-top gore, something that really spotlights lazy, ineffective writing when used in lesser works (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11775972.Crossed__volume_2_Family_values" title="Crossed, volume 2 Family values by David Lapham" rel="nofollow noopener">Crossed, volume 2: Family values</a> anyone). Oh, there’s plenty of blood and guts here, and some deeply disturbing “adult-orientated” sequences, but these scenes are used as impact accessories to the story, not the central attraction.<br><br>This graphic novel is creepy and unsettling in the way the best horror is. The story uses common, relatable life experiences (e.g., childhood fears, family dynamics, teenage awkwardness) as the canvas, upon which Hill and Rodriquez then layer some serious darkness, some well timed plot twists, and two exceptionally done villains, one human and one...other. <br><br>Okay..here’s a quick summary and some of the excellent artwork.<br><br><b><u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>:</b><br><br>In an act of brutal, seemingly random, violence, two teens murder Mr. Locke and shatter the lives of his wife and their three children, Ty, Kinsey and Bode. <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=LockeKeyPage2-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695164.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In the aftermath, the four travel to the town of Lovecraft, Massachusetts, to live at Key House, the families ancestral home. Each is broken in their own way, one by suffocating guilt, one by post traumatic shock, one by heartache and loneliness, and one by the loss of dad. <br><br>Unfortunately, the pain is not over.<br><br>Upon moving into Key House, things immediately take a turn for the weird. Turns out the Locke’s new home is neither ordinary ...<br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=Lockeghost-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695165.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>nor is it vacant. <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=LockeKey2page7-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695166.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>To make matters much, much worse, it also turns out that the murder of Mr. Locke was not random at all, and the family will find itself beset by nightmares both human and not human while they try and exorcise their grief and reassemble some semblance of a life. <br> <br><b><u>THOUGHTS</u>:</b><br><br>What makes this such a terrific story is not just the bounty of scary moments, some of which can really shake you. No, what sets this apart and is that Hill and Rodriguez tell a complete tale, and the calm, “ordinary” moments are as important, and as interesting, as the horror. <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=2cq05tw-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337714i/695167.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>One of my favorite of these moments is when Bode, testing out one of the houses many unusual attributes, secretly visits his sister as she relives the day their father died. <br><br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=21435sj-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380337715i/695168.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It is sad and moving, but ends comically in a perfect older sister, younger brother moment. It's perfect. <br><br>These quiet moments of reflection are necessary to heighten the emotional investment of the reader, and make the more aggressive events much scarier. <br><br>So, add this series to the ever growing pile of recent graphic novels that have really raised the bar. Series like <i>Preacher</i>, <i>The Walking Dead</i>, <i>Criminal</i>, <i>Sleeper</i>, <i>Incognito</i>, Sandman, <i>Gotham Central</i>...and now Locke &amp; Key. <br><br>Buy it...read it...love it. <br><br>4.5 stars. HIGHLY RECOMMENDED.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5032579015622518053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1188953362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1188953362" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1147139362?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1147139362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9999261922468184975">When I first started reading Locke & Key a couple years ago, I kinda shrugged and thought to myself, "Yeah. Okay. That's pretty good...." <br/><br/>But the story got its hooks into me pretty quickly after that. Unique concept. Great art. Great storytelling. Great characters. <br/><br/>I read a blurb somewhere that said something along the lines of, "Locke & Key is this generation's Sandman." I don't know if I'd go that far... but if someone wanted to take that stance around me, I don't think I'd waste much energy a</span>
  <span id="freeText9999261922468184975" style="display:none">When I first started reading Locke &amp; Key a couple years ago, I kinda shrugged and thought to myself, "Yeah. Okay. That's pretty good...." <br /><br />But the story got its hooks into me pretty quickly after that. Unique concept. Great art. Great storytelling. Great characters. <br /><br />I read a blurb somewhere that said something along the lines of, "Locke &amp; Key is this generation's Sandman." I don't know if I'd go that far... but if someone wanted to take that stance around me, I don't think I'd waste much energy arguing against it either. The truth is, this series does have a similar mythic feel to it, though its vibe is more Lovecraftian than folkloric. <br /><br />Simply said: great series. And as an added bonus, it stands entirely on its own. You don't need to know anything about Marvel continuity or folklore to help you understand the story. (Which might give it a leg up on Sandman in some ways.) <br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9999261922468184975" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1322743896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1322743896" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1322743896?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781600103841" href="/book/show/5594873-locke-key-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alejandro by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/34088223-gieliza">Gieliza</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=comic-book">comic-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1322743896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1636322007013911117"><b>
  <i>Fuck! ... That was an admiring “Fuck” not a “Fuck you” Fuck.</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><u>Creative Team:</u><br/><br/>Writer and Co-Creator: Joe Hill<br/><br/>Illustrator and Co-Creator: Gabriel Rodriguez<br/><br/>Coloring: Jay Fotos<br/><br/>Lettering: Robbie Robbins<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>KEY TO SUCCESS</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Welcome to Keyhouse, kid.</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Was it weird to grow up in a house with a name?</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>You have no idea.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I’ve heard a lot of good things about this comic book series, but...<br/><br/>...oh, boy! I never thought that it was <b>THAT GOOD</b>!!!<br/><br/>This first volume was really awesome!<br/><br/>The creative team, Hill & </span>
  <span id="freeText1636322007013911117" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Fuck! ... That was an admiring “Fuck” not a “Fuck you” Fuck.</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><u>Creative Team:</u><br /><br />Writer and Co-Creator: Joe Hill<br /><br />Illustrator and Co-Creator: Gabriel Rodriguez<br /><br />Coloring: Jay Fotos<br /><br />Lettering: Robbie Robbins<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>KEY TO SUCCESS</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Welcome to Keyhouse, kid.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Was it weird to grow up in a house with a name?</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>You have no idea.</i>
</b><br /><br />I’ve heard a lot of good things about this comic book series, but...<br /><br />...oh, boy! I never thought that it was <b>THAT GOOD</b>!!!<br /><br />This first volume was really awesome!<br /><br />The creative team, Hill &amp; Rodriguez, definitely they worked as a team, since the graphic sequences are beautiful synchronized between texts and drawings.<br /><br />Nothing is made by chance. Everything is carefully done. Writer and Artist aren’t in a competition of who’s bigger name in the title. Both are working in full communication to present a great story.<br /><br />In a prose novel is quite easy to “hide” stuff from the readers, if there isn’t written down, it doesn’t exist in their minds, but in a comic book, where it’s a visual format, you need to be crafty to “hide” things, and this creative team in the first chapter, they played with our expectations and each time that you think that you know what happened, a new piece of info is shown, telling you that it’s better to enjoy the ride and avoid to make assumptions.<br /><br />Of course, it doesn’t mean that you can guess here and there, future things in the tale, if you read carefully. Delicious reading.<br /><br />Joe Hill (Stephen King’s son) while he was already done prose work, this Project is his first venture in comic books, and certainly he did a masterful job.<br /><br />Gabriel Rodriguez’s art style reminds me like a merge between Frank Quitely’s and Humberto Ramos’. But don’t take me wrong, Rodriguez indeed has his own style and he did a superb task presenting a scary story, showing hard-to-cope scenes with elegance.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>KNOCK KNOCK</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Lots. Doors. To other worlds. Doors to other possibilities.</i>
</b><br /><br />You may think that the premise isn’t that original. True, it’s about a mysterious haunted house with magic doors. Something like <i>Narnia</i> or <i>Moving Castle</i> meets <i>Amityville</i>, but the <b>KEY</b> word here is...<br /><br />...Characters!<br /><br />Many stories may sound alike, many premises can born from similar ambiances, <b>BUT</b> the narrative element that they helped them to come out as distinctive tales are the characters and its developing. <br /><br />And you can be sure that this comic book has great characters with excellent development and wonderful interaction between each other. You can feel them as real people, and even when you think that you already figure it out some character, they always surprised and they become deeper and deeper, harder to know the turns that the story will take. Each chapter, while develops the general story, is beautiful managed to know deeper inside of certain character, a different one on each chapter. As I said before, nothing is made by chance, all it’s part of a well thought plan.<br /><br />A carefully crafted story where you aren’t getting into it at its beginning, and definitely not its ending neither!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1636322007013911117" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1231410663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186275514240954344">I could, as seems customary <b>in cases like this one</b> (where twenty thousand million people—and a half—loved a book but two—and one quarter—didn't), put one of those <s>silly</s> "<b>unpopular opinion</b>" warnings at the top of this review. <b>But I won't</b>. Ha. "Why," you ask? <b>Because</b>:<br/><br/><b>1</b>/ <b>Love a book? Hate a book</b>? Doesn't matter. It's your opinion, <b>you're entitled to it</b>. No need to apologize for <b>not agreeing</b> with the masses. Your opinion is what makes you YOU, so <b>bloody shrimping own it</b>. And stuff.<br/><b>2</b>/ <b>People who feel</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12186275514240954344" style="display:none">I could, as seems customary <b>in cases like this one</b> (where twenty thousand million people—and a half—loved a book but two—and one quarter—didn't), put one of those <s>silly</s> "<b>unpopular opinion</b>" warnings at the top of this review. <b>But I won't</b>. Ha. "Why," you ask? <b>Because</b>:<br><br><b>1</b>/ <b>Love a book? Hate a book</b>? Doesn't matter. It's your opinion, <b>you're entitled to it</b>. No need to apologize for <b>not agreeing</b> with the masses. Your opinion is what makes you YOU, so <b>bloody shrimping own it</b>. And stuff.<br><b>2</b>/ <b>People who feel offended</b> by those who dare criticize a book they love can <b>kiss my pincers</b>. <br><b>3</b>/ <b>I don't give a flying fish</b> what others think of my opinion.<br><b>4</b>/ <b>I'm in a great mood today</b>.<br><br><b>Soooooo, Locke &amp; Key</b>. I first tried reading this volume three years ago. I'd purchased the Kindle version but reading comics and graphic novels on a <b>tablet/computer/whatever</b> is not for me. What can I say, I'm one of those decrepit, ancient ones <b>who prefer good old paper over digitalized stuff</b>. Anyway, the <b>paperback version</b> was <s>a total rip off</s> 20€ at the time, so I decided to wait until the price went down and stuff. <b>And <s>now I wish I hadn't bothered</s> here we are</b>.<br><br><b>Okay, let's cut the crap and get this over with</b>:<br><br>① <b>I didn't like the art</b>. <br><b>Frankly</b>, I thought most of the characters looked <b>downright grotesque</b>. <br><br>There's the <b>Medusa wannabe who looks like a guy</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516290739i/24890556.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The teenager who <b>looks like a 40-year-old gorilla</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516291376i/24890574.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The P.E. teacher who has <b>Picasso-worthy hands and looks like a man</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516290739i/24890558.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The <b>guy with the rabbit teeth</b> who looks like he <b>might or might not be related</b> to the P.E. teacher of the Picasso-worthy hands:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516291376i/24890575.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And let's not forget <b>this delicious-looking lady</b> who's so bloody sexy I'm considering <b>locking her up in my harem</b>: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516290739i/24890559.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Long story short</b>: the characters are both <b>ugh and ew</b>. Also, their faces are too <b>pointy and angular</b>. Damn, <b>chins that sharp</b> should be outlawed or something. I mean, I'm pretty sure they're <b>more serrated and deadlier</b> than my murderous babies' pincers and stuff. Oh, before I forget: can someone tell me what the shrimp is up with <b>the shades on the characters' faces</b>? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516291815i/24890581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516290739i/24890557.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Please someone, anyone, get the poor boys a bucket of under eye concealer or something!</i><br><br><b>I could go on and on</b> about this lovely bunch, tell you about the super contagious <b>Snarly Mouth Virus</b> (SMV™) they're all obviously suffering from, or about <b>That Weird Semi Round Thing They Have on their Jagged Little Chins</b> (TWSRTTHotJLG™), but things to do, homicidal shrimps to unleash and all that crap, so I won't. <b>Lucky you and stuff</b>. One last thing I want to mention, though: there's <b>quite a lot of violence</b> in this volume. And <b>lots of blood, too</b>. This could have been most <b>delightfully gruesome</b>, had it not looked like someone kept inadvertently dropping <b>cans of tomato sauce</b> all over the panels. Kind of <b>takes the horror out of the horror story</b> and stuff. And makes the whole thing feel like a <b>ridiculous B movie</b>. But hey, it's not all bad. I mean, the art sort of <b>reminded me of a Gorillaz album</b>, which in turn reminded me of my glorious youth, so <b>yay and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516297761i/24890840.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>② <b>I didn't give a shrimping fish about any of the characters</b>.<br>Even lowly barnacles have <b>more charisma</b> that this unlikable bunch here. And my infamous herd of ironing boards is <b>way more emotional</b> than them, too. But what's really <b>depressing</b> here is that I didn't even <b>lust over the villains</b>. And that's quite suicide-inducing, <b>if you ask me</b>.<br><br>③ <b>I couldn't have cared less about the plot</b>.<br>It was <b>meh</b> and it was <b>sloooow</b> and it was <b>boring</b> and it was <b>all over the place</b> and it was <b>confusing as fish</b>. Only not in <b>Gloriously Befuddling Glen Cook Way</b> (GBGCW™). And I guess the story might have been appropriately <b>terrifying/sinister/macabre/whatever</b> if the art hadn't been so OTT as mentioned ↑↑. <b>But it was, so it wasn't</b>. Oh, and by the way, naming your <b>supposedly creepy</b> New England town Lovecraft isn't <b>particularly clever</b>. It's nothing more than <b>pretentious high-school level name-dropping</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1516298098ra/24890855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>» And the moral of this <b>This Graphic Novel is One of the Most Popular and Highest Rated on Goodreads This is it That Proves it The Fluffy Siberian Bunnies Have Hacked the Site This is the End Crappy Non Review</b> (TGNiOofMPaHRoGTisTPiTFSBHHtSTisECNR™) is: go ahead Locke &amp; Key maniacs, <b>unleash all hell</b> on me because I had the despicable audacity <b>not to fangirl about your precious</b>! I am not afraid and stuff! Also, <b>my murderous crustaceans are ready for you</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499506029ra/23240029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>April 2015</b>]<br><br><b>Note to self</b>: stop trying to read comics on your Kindle Fire. The screen is too small and the panels seem to have a life of their own (oh look! They zoom in and out all by themselves! It's magic!). Ugh. I guess I'll just have to wait for this to go on sale. Because there's no way I'm spending 20€ on a graphic novel. <b>Nope nope nope</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421607678ra/13391902.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12186275514240954344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4337324410530067886"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506372856i/24010386._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Going back and doing a reread of what I consider one of the best horror comics of all time. Joe Hill is Stephen King's son and Joe has definitely picked up some of his father's best traits. The story starts off tragically. Gabriel Rodriguez's art is so expressive. I felt myself getting all verklempt watching these kids deal with the awful aftermath of that day at the cottage. <br/><br/>So the family packs up and moves in with their uncle back at the family estate in Lovecraft, MA.   <span id="freeText4337324410530067886" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506372856i/24010386._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Going back and doing a reread of what I consider one of the best horror comics of all time. Joe Hill is Stephen King's son and Joe has definitely picked up some of his father's best traits. The story starts off tragically. Gabriel Rodriguez's art is so expressive. I felt myself getting all verklempt watching these kids deal with the awful aftermath of that day at the cottage. <br><br>So the family packs up and moves in with their uncle back at the family estate in Lovecraft, MA. As they are dealing with their loss while exploring this strange house, Bode comes across a key that allows him to open a door that allows only his spirit to go through. While ghosting around, he hears a voice in the wellhouse that slowly worms its way into getting Bode to do what it wants. Meanwhile, the boy who killed their father is slowly making his way across country to find the keys that have eluded him. And by the end of the book, everything is set up for the rest of the series.<br><br><br><b>Review of Season 1 of the Netflix TV show</b><br>Season 1 covers the first 3 volumes of the comics. The casting is spot on. The episodes were so-so though, especially the first half. It's obvious that some things were changed for budgetary reasons. The back half of the show does pick up. The show keeps with the major beats of the comics although the end of the first season does differ. Both Joe Hill and Gabriel Rodriguez make cameos in the last episode as paramedics. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589407804i/29470335._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589407804i/29470334._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you remember, Gabriel drew himself in as a paramedic at the beginning of <i>Alpha &amp; Omega</i>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589407804i/29470336._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All in all, it was a decent first season and I'll tune in for Season 2.</span>

<div id="review_3145815584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3145815584" />
    <a title="Nat K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35251024-nat-k"><img alt="Nat K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577481825p2/35251024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3145815584?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat K" href="/user/show/35251024-nat-k">Nat K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Nat by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3145815584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8822233100942535719"><br/><i>”If he does turn up, he better hope the cops get him. The next homicidal maniac who comes our way is going to be find another homicidal maniac waiting for him.”</i><br/><br/>A couple of admissions. I’ve not read a graphic novel in full before. I’ve only ever flicked through a couple at the bookstore and library. I’m not a fan of horror. This book is both. So, two firsts.<br/><br/><i>Lovecraft, Massachusetts</i>. The Rendell family have made the move back to the ancestral home “Keyhouse” in attempt to start life anew, after th</span>
  <span id="freeText8822233100942535719" style="display:none"><br /><i>”If he does turn up, he better hope the cops get him. The next homicidal maniac who comes our way is going to be find another homicidal maniac waiting for him.”</i><br /><br />A couple of admissions. I’ve not read a graphic novel in full before. I’ve only ever flicked through a couple at the bookstore and library. I’m not a fan of horror. This book is both. So, two firsts.<br /><br /><i>Lovecraft, Massachusetts</i>. The Rendell family have made the move back to the ancestral home “Keyhouse” in attempt to start life anew, after the shocking, violent murder of their husband/father, Rendell Locke. The family have escaped one horror, to find themselves embarking on another, as “Keyhouse” is filled with mysterious rooms and a mysterious inhabitant or two.<br /><br />While reading this, I couldn’t help but ponder why it seems that most graphic novels tend to veer toward darker themes. Very dark. Why is that? Maus (Klaus Spiegelmann), Batman: Dark Knight (Frank Miller), Sin City (Frank Miller) come to mind. Dark, dark and dark. I think the world has enough darkness in it, without adding more.<br /><br />I’m not saying I don’t appreciate the graphic novel as an art form. But I found this one to be excessively violent, and I just don’t see the point.<br /><br />The storyline which features the daughter, Kinsey, has some merit. Her feelings of isolation and guilt at her father’s death are well portrayed. Her wish to fit in at her new school, for people to stop staring at her because they know of her father’s gruesome death. Done with some insight into the teen mind.<br /><br />But the rest of the story did not resonate with me at all.<br /><br />Yes, Joe Hill can write. The talent for that particular art is definitely in his genes. I read his book “Heart Shaped Box” when it came out, and remember thinking at the time, it was pretty good for a first book. This particular storyline is just too harsh for me. It oozes malevolence and nastiness.<br /><br />Regarding the graphics, the colour (or lack thereof) is muted. Monochrome. Which adds to the tone of an already depressing storyline. Splodges of red dominate (too much blood). Gabriel Rodriguez’s images are sharp and help tell Joe Hills’s story well. Again, obviously a talented guy, but the content…<br /><br />While I appreciate the work that has gone into this graphic novel, it is not for me. Not my cup of tea at all. I won’t be continuing with the series.<br /><br /><b>STORYLINE: Joe Hill<br />ARTWORK: Gabriel Rodriguez</b><br /><br /><br /><i>Trigger Warning! </i> Excessive violence, bloody graphics, weapons, disturbing themes.<br /><br />*** Shout out to Dawn &amp; Ron who I buddy read this with. Make sure you have a look at their <br />thoughts about this book too. ***</span>
  <a data-text-id="8822233100942535719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254714435" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12188153355959498844">oooooo.... an eerie old mansion on a woody estate, strange mysteries and dangerous secrets, a tangled and forgotten past, a san francisco family of three - father slain - seeking a new life on an island named Lovecraft off the coast of massachusetts, in a place called The Keyhouse. a beautiful girl who lives at the bottom of a well, an insane killer on the hunt for magical keys, doors that open into odd places, walk through one door and change your gender, walk through another door and turn into</span>
  <span id="freeText12188153355959498844" style="display:none">oooooo.... an eerie old mansion on a woody estate, strange mysteries and dangerous secrets, a tangled and forgotten past, a san francisco family of three - father slain - seeking a new life on an island named Lovecraft off the coast of massachusetts, in a place called The Keyhouse. a beautiful girl who lives at the bottom of a well, an insane killer on the hunt for magical keys, doors that open into odd places, walk through one door and change your gender, walk through another door and turn into a ghost... who knows what else? the mysteries multiply. awesome! <br /><br />the art is excellent: a muted kind of vivid, smooth and professional, with a sometimes whimsical but basically grounded approach to illustrating the characters. and the writing is even better. characterization and narrative feel carefully honed, sketched with smaller strokes, intimate details parsed out slowly, the mysteries unfolding at an even pace, flashbacks that adroitly serve to both increase suspense and to render each character completely understandable, the narrative by turns sinister and endearing and magical - and always compelling both the quick turn of the page and the more contemplative search for hidden meaning in past pages.<br /><br />i really enjoyed this one a lot. i wish i had read it on Halloween. or on a rainy day in a creaky mansion on an island off of massachusetts. heaven!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9727952556467875400">I knew Joe Hill because I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539.NOS4A2' title='NOS4A2 by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>NOS4A2</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns' title='Horns by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Horns</a>, but discovered Locke and Key with the Netflix series. As I read in the reviews of the TV series, the graphic novels are darker and the plot is a bit different. For me, it was almost like reading another story, so it entertained me even if I just finished the show. I really like the universe Joe Hill created and I'm glad I can now read about it!</span>
  <span id="freeText9727952556467875400" style="display:none">I knew Joe Hill because I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539.NOS4A2" title="NOS4A2 by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">NOS4A2</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns" title="Horns by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Horns</a>, but discovered Locke and Key with the Netflix series. As I read in the reviews of the TV series, the graphic novels are darker and the plot is a bit different. For me, it was almost like reading another story, so it entertained me even if I just finished the show. I really like the universe Joe Hill created and I'm glad I can now read about it!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer982736268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9389302894208751037">After months of putting this aside, I finally decided to read this. The premise was very gripping, and the execution was adequate. It's not the best graphic novel I've ever read, but it does have the type of plot that would keep you reading till the end. I can't wait to read the second volume and find out what happens next.<br/><br/>Ups:<br/>-Fantastic plot<br/>-Likable Characters<br/>They all had their own problems, and each one resulted positively in terms of enjoyment. I enjoyed the graphic novel more because of that</span>
  <span id="freeText9389302894208751037" style="display:none">After months of putting this aside, I finally decided to read this. The premise was very gripping, and the execution was adequate. It's not the best graphic novel I've ever read, but it does have the type of plot that would keep you reading till the end. I can't wait to read the second volume and find out what happens next.<br /><br />Ups:<br />-Fantastic plot<br />-Likable Characters<br />They all had their own problems, and each one resulted positively in terms of enjoyment. I enjoyed the graphic novel more because of that because it added a feeling of psychological thriller to it.<br />-Decent Artwork<br />It could've been done better, but I've seen way worse. I'm not that fond of it, but it's something I can bear with.<br /><br />Downs:<br />-While the plot was fantastic, at times it was all over the place<br />-Contrary to my usual preference, I didn't like the shifting of timelines here. It was a bit confusing. Maybe it's because of the graphic novel format, but I didn't enjoy the shifting that much.<br /><br />4/5 stars.I heard that the series improves even more, so I'll be reading the next volumes real soon. While I was not blown away, I can still consider this a very good graphic novel. Highly recommended for horror and psycho-thriller fans.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_528177024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528177024" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/528177024?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=gn-horror">gn-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528177024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7664997295022835046">Great and engaging horror story by Joe Hill with great art to complement by Gabriel Rodriquez. I have not historically really been a horror fan, but this hooked me by focusing on the devastated Locke family that has to recover (and doesn't handle well, in each their own screwed-up ways) the murder of their father. We get to know and care about each of the characters, which I think for me must be the key to the best horror stories. Since we come to care about the people, and find them relatable s</span>
  <span id="freeText7664997295022835046" style="display:none">Great and engaging horror story by Joe Hill with great art to complement by Gabriel Rodriquez. I have not historically really been a horror fan, but this hooked me by focusing on the devastated Locke family that has to recover (and doesn't handle well, in each their own screwed-up ways) the murder of their father. We get to know and care about each of the characters, which I think for me must be the key to the best horror stories. Since we come to care about the people, and find them relatable small town folks, we suspend belief about their sometimes improbably suspenseful actions, and we keep turning the pages. And there's great dialogue, not just gore, though if you are looking for that, this story will not disappoint you. <br /><br />The series is a tribute to H. P. Lovecraft, obviously, from the subtitle. Of course the family moves into a perfect horror site, a dark and stormy gothic mansion named KeyHouse [too on-the-nose, these names?] with lots of secret rooms, each with a separate key and identity. Ghosts figure in this dark fantasy in interesting ways, of course, and the story thus works on different levels as most great stories do, delving into family and local history. As I said, I think the art is gorgeous, though there is a lot of use of red, as one might expect.... :) The impressive beginning to an important series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7664997295022835046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119589094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119589094?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=reviewed-3-stars">reviewed-3-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119589094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13827520086936772772">This book was (I imagine) what it might be like to down a spoonful of sugar that was, unbeknownst to you, <b>laced with Meth.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339031i/695881.jpg' width='310' height='440' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>What is IN this shi-at, Mary?!</i><br/><br/>The sugary spoonful sounds like a great idea in your head. "A house full of strange locks and doors with many keys that perform different astonishing feats. One door that can force your consciousness out of your body, while your body appears to be dead. A special key that can open any door and take you anywhere." Sounds great, right? Unfortunatel</span>
  <span id="freeText13827520086936772772" style="display:none">This book was (I imagine) what it might be like to down a spoonful of sugar that was, unbeknownst to you, <b>laced with Meth.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339031i/695881.jpg" width="310" height="440" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>What is IN this shi-at, Mary?!</i><br><br>The sugary spoonful sounds like a great idea in your head. "A house full of strange locks and doors with many keys that perform different astonishing feats. One door that can force your consciousness out of your body, while your body appears to be dead. A special key that can open any door and take you anywhere." Sounds great, right? Unfortunately, you get some disturbing surprises along with it. <i>A lot</i> of disturbing surprises.<br><br>In fact, I almost think that this book was actually <u>a spoonful of Meth laced with a dash of sugar</u>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339031i/695882.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Meth is my favorite thing!</i><br><br>I absolutely loved the little boy, Bode. As well as the storyline involving the creepy woman who lives in a locked-up well and calls herself an "echo". And the ripping-your-concious-out-of-your-body-for-fun door. <br><br>But EVERYTHING else, I didn't care for. And there's a lot going on. A little too much going on in fact.<br><br>I didn't appreciate the non-linear storytelling in this instance. Or the POV of the killer. Or even the art for the most part (except for Bode, his sister Kinsey, and the "Echo", which were really well done).<br><br><u>I probably would not recommend this to non-graphic novel readers.</u> Not until you are more experienced in the genre, at least.<br><br>It had a bit of adventure and a lot of fantasy. No romance and a lot of creepiness. There were definitely some very intriguing and awe-inspiring concepts but overall it was just a little too twisted.<br><br><i>Too much Meth and not enough sugar.</i><br><br><b>Like a crazy heat-seeking murdering alien maniac singing "These are a few of my Favorite Things."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339031i/695883.jpg" width="308" height="298" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="13827520086936772772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer39944521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6300779459060803297"><br/>Re-reading this for the third time as I get ready to tackle the final two volumes in the series: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13490570.Locke___Key__Vol5_Clockworks' title='Locke & Key, Vol5 Clockworks by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'> Clockworks</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16164271.Locke___Key__Vol6_Alpha___Omega' title='Locke & Key, Vol6 Alpha & Omega by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'> Alpha & Omega</a>. I love everything about the world and its rules Joe Hill has conjured here, and the characters he has lovingly crafted to live in its pages. <i>Locke & Key</i> has become one of my favorite series ever and I can't wait to see how it's going to end. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422932483i/13565634._SX540_.jpg' width='370' height='140' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/><b>2012 Review:</b><br/>This is my second go around with Joe Hill's phenomenal foray into graphic novel territory (to prepare for Volumes 3 </span>
  <span id="freeText6300779459060803297" style="display:none"><br>Re-reading this for the third time as I get ready to tackle the final two volumes in the series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13490570.Locke___Key__Vol5_Clockworks" title="Locke &amp; Key, Vol5 Clockworks by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener"> Clockworks</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16164271.Locke___Key__Vol6_Alpha___Omega" title="Locke &amp; Key, Vol6 Alpha &amp; Omega by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener"> Alpha &amp; Omega</a>. I love everything about the world and its rules Joe Hill has conjured here, and the characters he has lovingly crafted to live in its pages. <i>Locke &amp; Key</i> has become one of my favorite series ever and I can't wait to see how it's going to end. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422932483i/13565634._SX540_.jpg" width="370" height="140" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>2012 Review:</b><br>This is my second go around with Joe Hill's phenomenal foray into graphic novel territory (to prepare for Volumes 3 and 4). <i>Welcome to Lovecraft</i> is a stunning debut, and I enjoyed it even more this time, so much so that I've bumped it from four to five stars. Yes, it really is <i>that good</i>. <br><br>The premise is a fantastic one and you will be totally swept up in the awesome imagination it shows and the mystery and adventure it promises. The character development in just a few short pages is outstanding -- Hill deftly explores the wonderment of childhood, the searing pain of grief and the love of family. <br><br>Little Bode Locke is as sweet and precocious as they come. His boyish, unchecked curiosity is what reignites the mystery of Key House, the sprawling family mansion where the Locke family relocates after the brutal slaying of its patriarch. Left to grieve are big brother Ty, middle sister Kinsey, their mom, and of course Bode. <br><br>Each member of the family struggles to come to terms with the gargantuan loss -- Mom is drinking too much, Ty is crushed with guilt and contemplating suicide, Kinsey is withdrawn and tormented by the bloody memories of that fateful day. With his family so distracted, Bode is left to roam the grounds of Key House, and to become entangled in a very old mystery, like the fly unwittingly ensnared by the spider's web.<br><br>Key House is what it promises -- a house with many doors and with many keys to unlock them. I won't tell you what's behind the doors because that would ruin the surprise. I will say that it is so goddamn fantastic you are not going to be able to put this story down until you have finished it. Then you are going to want to run out and immediately get your hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/49478-locke-and-key" rel="nofollow noopener">the rest of the series</a> ... at least what Hill has written so far (and thank goodness he isn't done yet!)<br><br>This is storytelling at its <i>finest</i>. Can I use the word superlative? Yes? Alright, superlative.<br> <br><br><b>Original review December 2008</b><br>It's becoming clear to me that Joe Hill's real strength as a writer lies in the short story (and now graphic novel) format. There is obviously something about the concise, contained prose on a smaller canvas (rather than the sprawling novel) that brings out the best in his storytelling talents. I was not a fan of Hill's debut novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025.Heart_Shaped_Box" title="Heart-Shaped Box by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Heart-Shaped Box</a>; however, his short story collection <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373915.20th_Century_Ghosts" title="20th Century Ghosts by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">20th Century Ghosts</a> has amazing depth and texture, and he scores big again with <i>Locke and Key</i>, the first in a graphic novel series that shows real imagination. Calling the town Lovecraft is a nice touch. Let's not ignore the fantastic artistic contribution made by Gabriel Rodriquez. Their collaboration guarantees a memorable reading experience. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6300779459060803297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_939094494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939094494" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939094494?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15701190-locke-key-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939094494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14062608236286681022"><br/>This will be a rushed review, because :<br/>1)	I was too engrossed in the story to take notes, <br/>2)	I want to start on the second album as soon as possible.<br/><br/>The first thing I feel you need to know about the comic is that it is definitely a horror story, not for the faint of heart. Yes, the protagonists are very young, namely the three children of the Locke family, but I hesitate to call it Young Adult material, given the physical and psychological torments they are put through right from the start. Ther</span>
  <span id="freeText14062608236286681022" style="display:none"><br />This will be a rushed review, because :<br />1)	I was too engrossed in the story to take notes, <br />2)	I want to start on the second album as soon as possible.<br /><br />The first thing I feel you need to know about the comic is that it is definitely a horror story, not for the faint of heart. Yes, the protagonists are very young, namely the three children of the Locke family, but I hesitate to call it Young Adult material, given the physical and psychological torments they are put through right from the start. There’s also the explicit gore, the dialogue liberally laced with four letter words, the twisted look into the head of a psychopat that put the comic in the recommended for an adult audience bracket, at least for me.<br /><br />Having got the warning out of the way, let me say that Welcome to Lovecraft is one of the best written and best drawn comics I have read lately (and that includes The Sandman and Saga). I already knew about Joe Hill, and I have a couple of his books bought and waiting for the right mood to give them a chance, but even so I was pleasantly surprised by how well he handles the comic medium, how he mixes flashbacks and different points of view to transform the story of a horrible crime into a tale of supernatural forces battling for possession of mysterious artefacts hidden in a gothic mansion that pays homage to Edgar Alan Poe, Psycho the movie and Lovecraft. That’s actually the name of the mansion, on an island in Maine, but I’m also getting ahead of the story.<br /><br />The events start in California, where a couple of juvenile delinquents attack the Locke family leaving the father dead and the three children struggling to come to terms with the tragedy. Tyler is the eldest, seventeen or eighteen I believe, going trough the awkward phase were he rejects parental authority to the point where he feels guilty of pointing the killers at his father. Kinsey is twelve, a modern girl with a punk haircut and piercings, tough on the outside, but vulnerable and insecure inside. Bode is the youngest and most adventurous member of the family, at six still too young to understand all the implications of the events the family is going through. The mother herself emerges scarred and depressed from the ordeal, taking refuge in drink and moving the whole family to the East coast, to the mansion where most of the following events will take place.<br /><br />This mansion is a wonderful place to explore for young Bode and for the readers of the comic, thanks to the artwork of Gabriel Rodriguez. Bode finds the first of the magical keys with power to alter reality. He also meets a face-changer entity captive at the bottom of a well on the estate, possibly the mastermind of evil that is attacking the Locke family indirectly through mind controlled agents.<br /><br />Better stop here before I give the whole plot away. There is a lot of room for development in the next volumes, and I plan to read them as soon as I can get them in my hands. Luckily, the series is finished and I don’t have to wait years before the finish line, like I do with Saga.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14062608236286681022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2262332617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2262332617" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2262332617?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781600103841" href="/book/show/5594873-locke-key-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2262332617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer911900400824458566">I'm late as shit to the Joe Hill graphic novel game. I only read WRAITH because it was included in the limited edition of NOS4A2. I hate that I haven't started this series before now, but these shits are expensive. Rightly so, mind you, but I'm a professional writer, which means my income is limited. Plus I have a horrible (horrible in the best sense of the word) book addiction, so all of my fun money goes to novels and whatnot. This collection costs a hundred bones, but I managed to find a coll</span>
  <span id="freeText911900400824458566" style="display:none">I'm late as shit to the Joe Hill graphic novel game. I only read WRAITH because it was included in the limited edition of NOS4A2. I hate that I haven't started this series before now, but these shits are expensive. Rightly so, mind you, but I'm a professional writer, which means my income is limited. Plus I have a horrible (horrible in the best sense of the word) book addiction, so all of my fun money goes to novels and whatnot. This collection costs a hundred bones, but I managed to find a collector's edition on Amazon for sixty, so I finally snagged it. Super glad I did.<br /><br />Aside from some silly as fuck facial expressions, the artwork herein is pretty good. I especially like the designs of the keys and ethereal bodies. The book, in my opinion, is well put together, but there were places where I was confused as to whose head I was in. It wasn't until halfway through the book did I realize the inner-thought boxes were color coordinated with certain characters. At least I think that's how it works.<br /><br />I've yet to grow attached to any of the characters, given that the only thing I know about them is that they've suffered a terrible tragedy, but I'm hoping future books will further develop them. It's for this reason I dropped an entire star from my rating. <br /><br />The real draw here is the near-perfect tone of the piece and the rad story line. I appreciate that it went places I didn't expect, even if the bad guy did remind me a bit of the Gas Mask Man from NOS4A2. I'm hoping Hill has more than one kind of villain in his toolbox, because this kind of bad guy gets old real quick. <br /><br />In summation: LOCKE &amp; KEY: WELCOME TO LOVECRAFT is a solid read with good artwork throughout, even if some of the art made me laugh when I wasn't supposed to. I believe I prefer when Hill works with Charles Paul Wilson III, but that's entirely subjective.<br /><br />Final Judgment: Lock yourself in and turn the key.</span>
  <a data-text-id="911900400824458566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1686741445" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1686741445" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1686741445?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1686741445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3483145422320556003">Hey, hey, hey... this was a great little ghost story. You've got a big creepy house with interesting rooms to explore. You've got a family trying to rebuild their lives and start over. You've got keys to rooms where magical stuff happens. You've got keys that take you anywhere. You've got a psycho murderer with a rough past. You've got a scary something at the bottom of a well. Yeah, so if this kinda stuff is your jam then you will probably like this book, I mean comic book, I mean graphic novel</span>
  <span id="freeText3483145422320556003" style="display:none">Hey, hey, hey... this was a great little ghost story. You've got a big creepy house with interesting rooms to explore. You've got a family trying to rebuild their lives and start over. You've got keys to rooms where magical stuff happens. You've got keys that take you anywhere. You've got a psycho murderer with a rough past. You've got a scary something at the bottom of a well. Yeah, so if this kinda stuff is your jam then you will probably like this book, I mean comic book, I mean graphic novel. <br /><br />Joe Hill is very, very good at creating imaginative, expansive worlds and stories unlike anything else you've read. He takes horror stereotypes, puts them in a blender, and then uses them to create something very different and original. I'm excited to keep reading through these. <br /><br />Hey, you also get the added bonus of saying you read an entire book in one day until someone reminds you it's a graphic novel.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1397204442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1481568063050549686">A chili cheeseburger with avocado, tomatoes and jalapenos, there's plenty to sink your teeth into in Joe Hill's Locke & Key: Welcome to Lovecraft. It's a psychological horror story (not that the blood and gore isn't there in spades), but I feel like the characters are driven by guilt and tormented by what's missing from their lives. I enjoyed it. Not sure I will continue the series, even though the story became more compelling as it came to an end (of part 1). I do like my cheeseburgers, but I'm</span>
  <span id="freeText1481568063050549686" style="display:none">A chili cheeseburger with avocado, tomatoes and jalapenos, there's plenty to sink your teeth into in Joe Hill's Locke &amp; Key: Welcome to Lovecraft. It's a psychological horror story (not that the blood and gore isn't there in spades), but I feel like the characters are driven by guilt and tormented by what's missing from their lives. I enjoyed it. Not sure I will continue the series, even though the story became more compelling as it came to an end (of part 1). I do like my cheeseburgers, but I'm not sure I can survive a whole series on a diet of red meat! Fair warning: I'm going to begin my next couple of reviews with more comparisons to food. Maybe it will be fun or insightful or just plain silly, but I'm going with it! </span>
