        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270273362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7597530483730761571">When I put down <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns' title='Horns by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Horns</a>, I had a feeling I was going to be a Joe Hill fan. However, when I finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3217221.Locke_and_Key__Vol__1_Welcome_to_Lovecraft' title='Locke and Key, Vol. 1 Welcome to Lovecraft by Joe Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locke and Key, Vol. 1: Welcome to Lovecraft</a>, I traded that "feeling" in for a Joe Hill fanboy membership.<br/><br/>Good Gravy, this book was <b>spectacular</b>.<br/><br/>Granted, I had my reservations before cracking the cover (which I think I literally did when I dropped it on the floor of the library). Whenever I start a second book by an author I <i>reallllly</i> liked the first time around, my head fills with all these questions</span>
  <span id="freeText7597530483730761571" style="display:none">When I put down <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879.Horns" title="Horns by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Horns</a>, I had a feeling I was going to be a Joe Hill fan. However, when I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3217221.Locke_and_Key__Vol__1_Welcome_to_Lovecraft" title="Locke and Key, Vol. 1 Welcome to Lovecraft by Joe Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Locke and Key, Vol. 1: Welcome to Lovecraft</a>, I traded that "feeling" in for a Joe Hill fanboy membership.<br /><br />Good Gravy, this book was <b>spectacular</b>.<br /><br />Granted, I had my reservations before cracking the cover (which I think I literally did when I dropped it on the floor of the library). Whenever I start a second book by an author I <i>reallllly</i> liked the first time around, my head fills with all these questions. "Is it going to be as good as what I just read?" "Am I going to be letdown?" "Is there anyone that doesn't know he's Stephen King's son?" Thankfully, 2 out of those 3 questions were answered.<br /><br />This guy literally came out of no where for me. I knew who he was and had heard about the hype surrounding his work but for whatever reason, avoided him until recently. If anything, this graphic novel gives me another reason to branch out to comics that do not only feature dudes running around in tights.<br /><br />While I haven't exactly forgotten my experience with <b>Y: The Last Man</b> from last year, Hill has helped confirm the feeling I've had about non-superhero style storytelling. I've really been missing out on a genre of the format.<br /><br />Now begins the painful wait until Vol. 2 is in my hands.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2145396856881990233">I read this puppy when it first came out a few years ago and really wanted to like it, and didn’t. So, now the series is done, I thought I’d go back and give it another shot - maybe I was in the wrong frame of mind, or maybe I was just plain wrong, and this time I’d love it? Nope - still terrible, unfortunately.<br/><br/>Three kids - an older boy, his slightly younger sister, and their youngest sibling, a boy called Bode (and the only one whose name I could remember, purely for being such an odd name!) - </span>
  <span id="freeText2145396856881990233" style="display:none">I read this puppy when it first came out a few years ago and really wanted to like it, and didn’t. So, now the series is done, I thought I’d go back and give it another shot - maybe I was in the wrong frame of mind, or maybe I was just plain wrong, and this time I’d love it? Nope - still terrible, unfortunately.<br /><br />Three kids - an older boy, his slightly younger sister, and their youngest sibling, a boy called Bode (and the only one whose name I could remember, purely for being such an odd name!) - have their father taken from them when one of his students comes to his summer home and murders him. The kids and their mum move from west coast to east coast back to the father’s childhood home - a massive, forbidding Lovecraftian mansion in the fictional Massachusetts town of Lovecraft (the thinking seems to be: it’s a “horror” comic so let’s remind readers of it by heavily referencing horror writer, HP Lovecraft). <br /><br />The Lovecraftian mansion set in Lovecraft is of course haunted with all manner of ghosts and special keys unlock special doors that can warp space and time, even the temporal planes - when Bode walks through one door, his body is left behind and he becomes a ghost. And while the kids get over the trauma of their recent loss, their dad’s murderer is on the loose - and he’s coming to finish the job! <br /><br />It’s definitely cool that Joe Hill is following in his dad’s footsteps and writing his own haunted house story but I have to say he’s certainly not as great a writer as Stephen King was when he was a younger man and Locke &amp; Key isn’t a patch on The Shining. For one, Hill focuses far too much on the kids’ difficulty in getting over their dad’s death which is realistic but not at all compelling to read - I get it, they’re saaaaaaaad! - while failing to make them stand out as characters. <br /><br />The older brother is pure emo, the sister is a flatliner - she literally at one point joins a track team and says that she’s running because she’s got a lot to run away from - what cheesy writing! - and Bode is your average Disney kid. Cute as a bug, always being clumsy but in a way that advances the story like he’s fooling around and then - oh, is that a special key that fell out of that jug I knocked off that shelf? How convenient! <br /><br />And how on earth can this family afford so much? They have a summer home, separate from their regular home, AND a giant mansion on the other side of the country! Their mum doesn’t work, their dad was a school administrator, and the uncle is a failed artist. Where the hell is the money coming from!? <br /><br />The story is completely static. The kids mope about - do we like them yet now that we’ve seen them sob for the millionth time? not even a bit! - while Bode pokes about the mansion and stumbles across the magic doorways and the ghost in the well. Basically the story is, the family moves to the mansion and then spends the whole book waiting for the killer to show up - very boring! <br /><br />I do appreciate the supernatural element and that the keys and doors thing is original, but the book really needs things like a plot and characters you care about in order for it to matter. Bode becomes a ghost, then the older brother - so what? I hate both of these clods! <br /><br />Gabriel Rodriguez’s art is fine but I don’t think it’s suited to the horror genre, mostly because it’s too cartoonish. The characters are a little too anime-esque for Hill’s over-emotional, horror-leaning script and I can’t say I found the villains in the story very menacing in their depiction. The layouts and drawings themselves are fine and definitely suit mainstream comics, but for a comic that’s supposed to creep you out, it’s not a good fit. <br /><br />I’ve tried reading one other Joe Hill book, Heart Shaped Box, which I couldn’t get past page 50 because it was so badly written, so I guess his work just isn’t for me. <br /><br />Locke &amp; Key wants to be a horror comic that mixes the old and new to create something exciting and fresh, but instead it’s a very tedious book with completely flat characters, a slow and uninvolving plot, and some supernatural elements that don’t liven up the paper-thin story in the least. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2145396856881990233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4856017503763444577"><b>★★★★☆½</b><br/><br/>And now, my second dip into the shallow end. I had so much fun with my initial venture, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/146415-saga-collected-editions' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saga</a>, that I was more than willing to test out the waters once again.<br/> <br/>Well, you can go ahead and mark me down as two for two because this shit was fantastic!   <span id="freeText4856017503763444577" style="display:none"><b>★★★★☆½</b><br /><br />And now, my second dip into the shallow end. I had so much fun with my initial venture, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/146415-saga-collected-editions" rel="nofollow noopener">Saga</a>, that I was more than willing to test out the waters once again.<br /> <br />Well, you can go ahead and mark me down as two for two because this shit was fantastic! The only criticism I could even level is that the writing felt a bit clunky here and there. But honestly, when I looked back over a few of the sections I had an issue with they seemed okay. Once again the artwork is top-notch. Perhaps the spooky mansion is a little cliché, along with all the nods to HP Lovecraft, but overall, the storyline is very intriguing with keys that open to so many possibilities. <br /><br />That's really all I care to say on the matter. I don't want to spoil any plot points for those of you who've yet to check this out. But I would urge all of you to do so immediately!<br /><br />Thank God I have all the other volumes queued up. I'm really excited to see how this all shakes out. <br /><br />4.5 Stars, rounded down.</span>

<div id="review_1963455284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963455284" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963455284?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=graphic-novels-manga-comics">graphic-novels-manga-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963455284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11204020096655302883">I love - no, really, <i>love</i> Joe Hill's writing. I think he has a beautifully wicked imagination, and to be frank, I believe that even the man's <i>grocery lists</i> are probably strange.<br/><br/>Like everything else I have read by Joe, the story line was simultaneously sad, unsettling, and downright odd; however, the icing on the cake came from Gabriel Rodriguez's <i>gorgeous</i> illustrations. From the front cover to the back, each panel was just captivating, with brilliant color schemes and mind-blowing attention to d</span>
  <span id="freeText11204020096655302883" style="display:none">I love - no, really, <i>love</i> Joe Hill's writing. I think he has a beautifully wicked imagination, and to be frank, I believe that even the man's <i>grocery lists</i> are probably strange.<br /><br />Like everything else I have read by Joe, the story line was simultaneously sad, unsettling, and downright odd; however, the icing on the cake came from Gabriel Rodriguez's <i>gorgeous</i> illustrations. From the front cover to the back, each panel was just captivating, with brilliant color schemes and mind-blowing attention to detail. Artistically speaking, this was by far one of the most enjoyable graphic novels I've had the pleasure of reading.<br /><br />As far as the story goes, where do I begin? It's devastatingly sad, in parts; right off the bat, we're dealing with a couple of kids who have just watched a classmate murder their father, and to make matters worse, the big brother of the crew blames himself for every bit of it. His guilt is positively tangible, as is the sense of loss their mother drowns in spirits, or the desperation to go unnoticed that his previously free-spirited younger sister falls into.<br /><br />Beyond the sadness, there's just a fantastic sense of dread from start to finish, and that's got to be one of my favorite qualities to Joe's writing. Once the action really got going, I was on the edge of my seat through to the very end. I found myself rooting so hard for the Locke kids, especially little Bode, who was just adorable and zany and loving.<br /><br />I would recommend this to any horror lover - especially those who love Joe Hill's quirky writing as much as I do.<br /><br /><b>Series content warning: violence, sexual assault, homophobia, racism, sexism, ableism.</b> All negative views are challenged by the text, but are very present.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11204020096655302883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x37L2Rdndgt4Yyqnf3Ormr2/4DKmt1ox7ZrjwRaxptdnJg19aNPkeFWksVM5mVqa+kQirRjr++X5DgEQ4HqxaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OV4jW/86jxHv01BZ/4ZCbFgayLXfs5tf6cFFKO/OqJ6ZBuX/gI4dYsIUy625bLNsH+EKKmHvOov9Vaf5GQW/IQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15147663564218611151">Joe Hill's debut, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box' title=' Heart-Shaped Box' rel='nofollow noopener'> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns' title=' Horns' rel='nofollow noopener'> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2' title=' NOS4A2' rel='nofollow noopener'> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman' title=' The Fireman' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br/><br/>He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in </span>
  <span id="freeText15147663564218611151" style="display:none">Joe Hill's debut, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153025._Heart_Shaped_Box" title=" Heart-Shaped Box" rel="nofollow noopener"> Heart-Shaped Box</a>, won the Bram Stoker Award for Best First Novel. His second,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6587879._Horns" title=" Horns" rel="nofollow noopener"> Horns</a>, was made into a film freakfest starring Daniel Radcliffe. His other novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15729539._NOS4A2" title=" NOS4A2" rel="nofollow noopener"> NOS4A2</a>, and his #1 New York Times Best-Seller, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25816688._The_Fireman" title=" The Fireman" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Fireman</a>... which was also the winner of a 2016 Goodreads Choice Award for Best Horror Novel.<br /><br />He writes short stories too. Some of them were gathered together in his prize-winning collection, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373915._20th_Century_Ghosts" title=" 20th Century Ghosts" rel="nofollow noopener"> 20th Century Ghosts</a>.<br /><br />He won the Eisner Award for Best Writer for his long running comic book series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26225895._Locke___Key" title=" Locke &amp; Key" rel="nofollow noopener"> Locke &amp; Key</a>, co-created with illustrator and art wizard Gabriel Rodriguez.<br /><br />He lives in New Hampshire with a corgi named McMurtry after a certain beloved writer of cowboy tales. His next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30251972._Strange_Weather" title=" Strange Weather" rel="nofollow noopener"> Strange Weather</a>, a collection of novellas, storms into bookstores in October of 2017.<br /></span>
